From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia

The **2012 Pacific typhoon season** was a slightly above average season that produced 25 named storms, fourteen typhoons, and four intense typhoons. It was the second consecutive season to be a deadly and destructive season, primarily due to [Typhoon Bopha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Bopha "Typhoon Bopha") which killed 1,901 people in the [Philippines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippines "Philippines"). It was an event in the annual cycle of [tropical cyclone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_cyclone "Tropical cyclone") formation, in which tropical cyclones form in the western Pacific Ocean. The season ran throughout 2012, though most tropical cyclones typically [develop](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_cyclogenesis "Tropical cyclogenesis") between May and October. The season's first named storm, Pakhar, developed on March 28, while the season's last named storm, Wukong, dissipated on December 29. The season's first typhoon, Guchol, reached typhoon status on June 15, and became the first super typhoon of the year on June 17.

The scope of this article is limited to the Pacific Ocean, to the north of the [equator](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equator "Equator") between [100°E](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/100th_meridian_east "100th meridian east") and the [180th meridian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/180th_meridian "180th meridian"). Within the northwestern Pacific Ocean, there are two separate agencies that assign names to tropical cyclones, which can often result in a cyclone having two names. The [Japan Meteorological Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency "Japan Meteorological Agency")(JMA) will name a tropical cyclone should it be judged to have 10-minute [sustained wind speeds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maximum_sustained_wind "Maximum sustained wind") of at least 65 km/h (40 mph) anywhere in the basin. PAGASA assigns unofficial names to tropical cyclones which move into or form as a tropical depression in their area of responsibility, located between 115°E–135°E and between 5°N–25°N, regardless of whether or not a tropical cyclone has already been given a name by the JMA. Tropical depressions that are monitored by the United States' [Joint Typhoon Warning Center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center "Joint Typhoon Warning Center")(JTWC) are given a numerical designation with a "W" suffix.

Seasonal forecasts
------------------

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=1 "Edit section: Seasonal forecasts")]

| Agency | Date | Tropical storms | Total Typhoons | Intense TCs [[nb 1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-2) | Ref |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| TSR | April 13, 2012 | 25.5 | 15.6 | 7.3 | [[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-TSR_April-3) |
| STI | April 26, 2012 | 22- 24 | - | - | [[1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-TSR_May-1) |
| TSR | May 4, 2012 | 25.5 | 15.6 | 8.5 | [[1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-TSR_May-1) |
| CWB | June 29, 2012 | 23- 26 | - | - | [[3]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-CWB-4) |
| TSR | July 9, 2012 | 26.8 | 16.7 | 9.2 | [[4]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-TSR_July-5) |
| TSR | August 6, 2012 | 27.4 | 17.4 | 9.3 | [[5]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-TSR_August-6) |
|  | Forecast Center | Tropical storms | Typhoons | Ref |
| **Actual activity**: | JMA | 25 | 14 | [[6]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-7) |
| **Actual activity**: | JTWC | 25 | 16 | [[7]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-8) |

During February 2012, the Pacific El Niño/Southern Oscillation Applications Climate (PEAC) Center predicted that the first half of 2012 would see below-normal tropical cyclone activity, as the [2010–2012 La Niña event](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010%E2%80%932012_La_Ni%C3%B1a_event "2010–2012 La Niña event") would prevent the monsoon trough of low pressure from developing normally and any major activity until June.[[8]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-PEU_Q1_2012-9) They also suggested that weather patterns would return to near-normal afterwards and that the westward displacement of systems seen in the previous two seasons would not occur.[[8]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-PEU_Q1_2012-9) On March 20, the [Hong Kong Observatory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hong_Kong_Observatory "Hong Kong Observatory") predicted that the typhoon season in Hong Kong and surrounding areas would likely start in June as a result of the La Niña event. They also predicted that between 5 and 8 systems would pass within 500 km (310 mi) of the territory and possibly impact the territory.[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-10) On April 11, the Tropical Storm Risk Consortium (TSR) issued its first seasonal forecast for the year, which predicted that the basin would be about 10% below average and feature 25.5 tropical storms, 15.6 typhoons, 7.3 intense typhoons.[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-TSR_April-3) This was followed later that month by the Shanghai Typhoon Institute (STI), who predicted that between 22 and 24 tropical storms would develop within the basin during the year before TSR tweaked its forecast in May and predicted that the season would be near-normal and feature 8.5 intense typhoons.[[1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-TSR_May-1)

On May 21, the [Thai Meteorological Department](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thai_Meteorological_Department "Thai Meteorological Department") predicted that 1-2 tropical storms would affect Thailand during 2012, with one moving through Vietnam and impacting upper Thailand during August or September, while the other one was expected to impact southern Thailand during October or November.[[10]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-11) On June 29, Taiwan's Central Weather Bureau (CWB) noted that sea surface temperatures had been gradually increasing and that there was a 50% chance of an El Nino event developing in the Pacific Ocean during the year.[[3]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-CWB-4) They also noted that systems tended to develop further away from Taiwan, had a longer lifespan and a greater intensity during El Nino events and urged citizens and local authorities to prepare.[[3]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-CWB-4) The CWB also predicted that 23 to 26 systems would occur over the basin during the year, of which three to five were expected to impact the island nation.[[3]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-CWB-4) Within its July update, TSR significantly increased its forecast as a result of the warmer sea surface temperatures and now predicted that the basin would see activity about 10% above average with 27.4 tropical storms, 16.7 typhoons, 9.2 intense typhoons.[[4]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-TSR_July-5) Within its July— December seasonal climate outlook, PAGASA predicted that 7— 10 tropical cyclones were likely to develop within or enter the Philippine area of responsibility between July and September, while 4— 7 were predicted to occur between October and December.[[11]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-PAG_2-12)

Season summary
--------------

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=2 "Edit section: Season summary")]

See also: [Timeline of the 2012 Pacific typhoon season](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_the_2012_Pacific_typhoon_season "Timeline of the 2012 Pacific typhoon season")

![Image 6](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/d4mwi3br8p2dixnas4y4ov2irfaimd1.png)

Costliest known Pacific typhoon seasons | Rank | Total damages | Season |
| --- | --- | --- |
| 1 | $38.54 billion | [2019](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2019_Pacific_typhoon_season "2019 Pacific typhoon season") |
| 2 | $37.83 billion | [2023](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2023_Pacific_typhoon_season "2023 Pacific typhoon season") |
| 3 | $30.6 billion | [2018](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2018_Pacific_typhoon_season "2018 Pacific typhoon season") |
| 4 | $29.62 billion | [2024](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_Pacific_typhoon_season "2024 Pacific typhoon season") |
| 5 | $26.45 billion | [2013](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2013_Pacific_typhoon_season "2013 Pacific typhoon season") |
| 6 | $21.05 billion | [2012](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season) |
| 7 | $18.77 billion | [2004](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2004_Pacific_typhoon_season "2004 Pacific typhoon season") |
| 8 | $17.44 billion | [1991](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1991_Pacific_typhoon_season "1991 Pacific typhoon season") |
| 9 | $16.96 billion | [2016](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016_Pacific_typhoon_season "2016 Pacific typhoon season") |
| 10 | $15.1 billion | [2017](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017_Pacific_typhoon_season "2017 Pacific typhoon season") |

As the year opened, the [Japan Meteorological Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency "Japan Meteorological Agency") was monitoring a tropical depression that was located about 345 km (215 mi) to the northeast of Kuala Lumpur, Malaysia; however, the system was last noted later that day as it dissipated.[[12]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-13)[[13]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-14)

On January 13, the JMA started monitoring a tropical depression that was located within an area of moderate to strong vertical windshear about 625 km (390 mi) to the east of [Kuala Lumpur](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur "Kuala Lumpur") in Malaysia.[[14]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-15)[[15]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-16) During that day the depression remained near stationary, before the JMA issued their final advisory on the system during the next day as the system dissipated.[[16]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-17)[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-18)[[18]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-19)

The season's first named storm, Pakhar, developed on March 28 while the last named storm, Wukong, dissipated on December 29. The season became very active between mid-July and mid-August, with nine named storms formed during the period. [Vicente](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Vicente_(2012) "Typhoon Vicente (2012)") underwent [explosive intensification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rapid_deepening#Explosive_intensification "Rapid deepening") and made landfall over the west [Pearl River Delta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pearl_River_Delta "Pearl River Delta") as a strong typhoon. [Damrey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Damrey_(2012) "Typhoon Damrey (2012)") developed into a typhoon in the [Yellow Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yellow_Sea "Yellow Sea") and became the most intense tropical cyclone to make landfall north of the [Yangtze River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yangtze_River "Yangtze River") since 1949. [Typhoon Haikui](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Haikui_(2012) "Typhoon Haikui (2012)"), although centred far away from the [Philippines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippines "Philippines"), killed at least 89 people in the country. [Typhoon Tembin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Tembin_(2012) "Typhoon Tembin (2012)") affected [Taiwan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taiwan "Taiwan") twice because of its cyclonic loop.

From late August to September, three very powerful typhoons, [Bolaven](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Bolaven_(2012) "Typhoon Bolaven (2012)"), [Sanba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Sanba "Typhoon Sanba") and [Jelawat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Jelawat_(2012) "Typhoon Jelawat (2012)"), directly hit [Okinawa Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Okinawa_Island "Okinawa Island") successively. In October, the remnants of Severe Tropical Storm Gaemi arrived at the [Bay of Bengal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bay_of_Bengal "Bay of Bengal") and re-intensified into a [deep depression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_North_Indian_Ocean_cyclone_season#Deep_Depression_BOB_01 "2012 North Indian Ocean cyclone season") before making landfall over [Bangladesh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bangladesh "Bangladesh"). In December, [Typhoon Bopha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Bopha "Typhoon Bopha"), an unusually very low-latitude but very powerful tropical cyclone, caused catastrophic damage in [Mindanao](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mindanao "Mindanao") in the [Philippines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippines "Philippines").

Systems
-------

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=3 "Edit section: Systems")]

### Tropical Depression 01W

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=4 "Edit section: Tropical Depression 01W")]

Tropical depression(JMA)
Tropical depression(SSHWS)
[![Image 7](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/01W_Feb_19_2012_0530Z.jpg/250px-01W_Feb_19_2012_0530Z.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:01W_Feb_19_2012_0530Z.jpg)[![Image 8](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/01W_2012_track.png/250px-01W_2012_track.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:01W_2012_track.png)
Duration February 17– February 21
Peak intensity 55 km/h (35 mph) (10-min);

1004[hPa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit) "Pascal (unit)")([mbar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(unit) "Bar (unit)"))

Early on February 17, the JMA reported that a tropical depression had developed, about 800 km (495 mi) to the southeast of [Manila](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manila "Manila") on the [Philippine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippine "Philippine") island of [Luzon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luzon "Luzon").[[19]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-20) During that day the depression moved westwards, before the Joint Typhoon Warning Center initiated advisories at 1500 UTC and designated the system as Tropical Depression 01W.[[20]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-21) However, six hours later the JTWC issued its final advisory as vertical windshear had started to increase, and after it had found no deep convection near the systems low level circulation centre during a reassessment of the depressions low level structure.[[21]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-22) Over the next few days the JMA continued to monitor the depression before it was last noted during February 20.[[22]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-23)

### Tropical Storm Pakhar

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=5 "Edit section: Tropical Storm Pakhar")]

Tropical storm(JMA)
Tropical storm(SSHWS)
[![Image 9](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Pakhar_2012-03-30.jpg/250px-Pakhar_2012-03-30.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Pakhar_2012-03-30.jpg)[![Image 10](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Pakhar_2012_track.png/250px-Pakhar_2012_track.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Pakhar_2012_track.png)
Duration March 26– April 2
Peak intensity 75 km/h (45 mph) (10-min);

986[hPa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit) "Pascal (unit)")([mbar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(unit) "Bar (unit)"))

Main article: [Tropical Storm Pakhar (2012)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Pakhar_(2012) "Tropical Storm Pakhar (2012)")

On March 24, the JMA reported that a tropical depression had formed, about 250 mi (400 km) to the southwest of Manila, Philippines.[[23]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-24) It later weakened to a low pressure area late on the same day.[[24]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-25) Two days later, the JMA upgraded the tropical disturbance back to a tropical depression again, due to the storm reorganizing under an environment of low vertical wind shear and favorable sea surface temperatures in the [South China Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_China_Sea "South China Sea").[[25]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-26)[[26]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-27) Early on March 28, the JTWC issued a TCFA on the tropical depression.[[27]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-28) By the next day, the JMA upgraded the tropical depression to a tropical storm, and named it _Pakhar_.[[28]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-29) The JTWC subsequently started issuing advisories on the storm, as the storm's convection had completely wrapped around the circulation center.[[29]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-30) The JTWC later upgraded Pakhar into a tropical storm.[[30]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-31)

Early on March 30, the JTWC upgraded Pakhar to a Category 1 typhoon, as a banding [eye](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eye_(cyclone) "Eye (cyclone)") formed; post-analysis later showed that Pakhar didn't reach typhoon intensity.[[31]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-32)[[32]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-IBTRACS_Pakhar-33) Because of land interaction and colder sea surface temperatures, Pakhar weakened to a tropical storm by the next day.[[33]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-34) On April 1, Pakhar made landfall near [Vũng Tàu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/V%C5%A9ng_T%C3%A0u "Vũng Tàu"), [Vietnam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vietnam "Vietnam").[[34]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-35) As it weakened into a tropical depression, the JMA issued their final advisory by the next day.[[35]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-36) The system was last noted over Cambodia that same day.[[36]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-37)

Although Pakhar did not affect the Philippines as a tropical cyclone, its precursor produced heavy rains across part of the nation. Flooding occurred in different parts of central and southern [Luzon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luzon "Luzon"), and the northern [Visayas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Visayas "Visayas") region.[[37]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-38) In Basud, Camarines Norte, 128 families had to be evacuated due to flash flooding. A few landslides resulted from the rains, damaging or destroying a few homes. Throughout the affected region, five people were killed and three others were listed as missing.[[38]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-PakharNDRRMC9-39) In Vietnam, ten people were killed and several others were injured due to flash flooding and high winds. The hardest hit area was [Khánh Hòa Province](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kh%C3%A1nh_H%C3%B2a_Province "Khánh Hòa Province") where the storm made landfall. About 4,400 homes were damaged in the region by the storm and thousands of acres of rice paddy were flooded.[[39]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-PakharEarthweek-40) In [Ho Chi Minh City](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ho_Chi_Minh_City "Ho Chi Minh City"), officials reported that 600 homes and schools were destroyed.[[40]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-41) Total damage were finalized at [₫](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vietnamese_%C4%91%E1%BB%93ng "Vietnamese đồng")1.12 trillion (US$53.9 million).[[41]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-VNCHMFReport-42) The remnants of the system brought rains to parts of [Cambodia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cambodia "Cambodia"), [Laos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Laos "Laos"), and [Thailand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thailand "Thailand").[[39]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-PakharEarthweek-40)

### Severe Tropical Storm Sanvu

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=6 "Edit section: Severe Tropical Storm Sanvu")]

Severe tropical storm(JMA)
Category 1 typhoon(SSHWS)
[![Image 11](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Sanvu_2012-05-25.jpg/250px-Sanvu_2012-05-25.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sanvu_2012-05-25.jpg)[![Image 12](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Sanvu_2012_track.png/250px-Sanvu_2012_track.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sanvu_2012_track.png)
Duration May 20– May 27
Peak intensity 110 km/h (70 mph) (10-min);

975[hPa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit) "Pascal (unit)")([mbar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(unit) "Bar (unit)"))

On May 18, the JTWC started to monitor an area of convection approximately 95 nmi (175 km) to the north-northwest of [Chuuk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chuuk_State "Chuuk State"). At the time, it had a developing low-level circulation center with deep convection, and was under an environment of low vertical wind shear and good divergence aloft.[[42]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-43) As it moved northwestwards, it continued to organize, prompting the JTWC to issue a TCFA two days later.[[43]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-44)[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-45) The JMA subsequently upgraded the system to a tropical depression on May 21.[[45]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-46) The JTWC later followed suit, designating the depression as 03W.[[46]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-47) The system then intensified to a tropical storm late on the same day, with the JMA naming it as _Sanvu_ early on May 22.[[47]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-48)[[48]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-49) Sanvu then continued to intensify, with deep convection building over its center.[[49]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-50)

Late on the next day, the JTWC upgraded Sanvu to a category 1 typhoon, as an eye was seen on microwave imagery.[[50]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-51) Late on May 24, the JMA upgraded Sanvu to a severe tropical storm.[[51]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-52) Accelerating northeastward along the northwestern periphery of a subtropical ridge, the system reached its peak intensity by the next day, as its eye emerged on satellite imagery.[[52]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-53)[[53]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-54)[[54]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-55) As its western quadrant got affected by a dry air entrainment on May 26, Sanvu started to weaken as it directly passed over [Iwo Jima](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iwo_Jima "Iwo Jima").[[55]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-56) With strong vertical wind shear associated with a subtropical jet stream, along with rapidly cooling sea surface temperatures, the system continued to weaken.[[56]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-57) The JTWC downgraded Sanvu to a tropical storm late on the same day, as the system's low level circulation center started to become exposed.[[57]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-58) The JMA followed suit by the next day.[[58]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-59) The JTWC subsequently issued their final advisory on Sanvu, as it commenced [extratropical transition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extratropical_transition "Extratropical transition").[[59]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-60) However, the JMA continued issuing advisories on Sanvu, until by the next day, when it fully transitioned into an extratropical cyclone.[[60]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-61)[[61]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-62) The remnants of the system was last noted during May 30.[[62]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-Sanvu_BT-63)

As Sanvu strengthened into a tropical storm, tropical storm watches and warnings were issued for [Guam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guam "Guam"), [Rota](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rota_(island) "Rota (island)"), [Tinian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tinian "Tinian"), and [Saipan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saipan "Saipan").[[63]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-64) It brought tropical storm force wind gusts and rainfall between 38–51 mm (1.5–2 in) to parts of Guam and the Northern Mariana Islands. However, the only damage reported was on Guam where falling tree limbs caused an estimated $20,000 of damage to power lines.[[64]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-Sanvu_NCDC-65)

### Typhoon Mawar (Ambo)

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=7 "Edit section: Typhoon Mawar (Ambo)")]

Typhoon(JMA)
Category 3 typhoon(SSHWS)
[![Image 13](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Mawar_Jun_4_2012_0430Z.jpg/250px-Mawar_Jun_4_2012_0430Z.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Mawar_Jun_4_2012_0430Z.jpg)[![Image 14](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Mawar_2012_track.png/250px-Mawar_2012_track.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Mawar_2012_track.png)
Duration May 31– June 6
Peak intensity 140 km/h (85 mph) (10-min);

960[hPa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit) "Pascal (unit)")([mbar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(unit) "Bar (unit)"))

Main article: [Typhoon Mawar (2012)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Mawar_(2012) "Typhoon Mawar (2012)")

On May 29, the JTWC started to monitor a tropical disturbance that formed approximately 125 nmi (230 km) to the north of [Palau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palau "Palau"). At the time, the system had a weak low-level circulation center, and was under an environment of low to moderate vertical wind shear and good divergence aloft.[[65]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-66) As the disturbance began moving northwestwards, it started to organize, with deep convection building along its developing center.[[66]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-67) Late on the next day, the system's convection became significantly organized, prompting the JTWC to issue a TCFA.[[67]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-68) By May 31, the JMA had upgraded the system to a tropical depression.[[68]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-69) The [PAGASA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PAGASA "PAGASA") followed suit and started issuing advisories on the system, assigning its local name _Ambo_.[[69]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-70) Late on the same day, the JTWC began issuing advisories on the system as it continued to consolidate its center, designating it as 04W.[[70]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-71) By the next day, Ambo intensified into a tropical storm, with the JMA assigning its international name _Mawar_.[[71]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-72)[[72]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-73)

With warm sea surface temperatures and decreasing wind shear, Mawar developed a [central dense overcast](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_dense_overcast "Central dense overcast").[[73]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-74) This led to the JMA upgrading Mawar to a severe tropical storm on June 2.[[74]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-75) The JTWC subsequently upgraded it to a Category 1 typhoon as a developing eye feature was seen on microwave imagery.[[75]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-76) Turning northeastward as a mid-latitude trough weakened the subtropical ridge to the northeast, Mawar further intensified into a Category 2 typhoon early on the next day, as a ragged eye became visible on satellite imagery.[[76]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-77) The JMA followed suit and upgraded Mawar to a typhoon later that same day.[[77]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-78) By June 4, Mawar reached its peak intensity,[[78]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-79)[[79]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-80) before it started to weaken due to the mid-latitudes impacting the system's overall structure, with its eye breaking down into tight spiral banding, prompting the JTWC to downgrade the system to a category 2 typhoon.[[80]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-81) On the next day, the PAGASA issued their final advisory on Mawar, as it was exiting the [Philippine Area of Responsibility](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippine_Area_of_Responsibility "Philippine Area of Responsibility").[[81]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-82) Mawar further weakened into a category 1 typhoon as its low-level circulation center widened, and was entering a hostile environment due to its interaction with the jet stream.[[82]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-83) The JMA subsequently downgraded Mawar to a severe tropical storm,[[83]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-84) as it commenced its extratropical transition.[[84]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-85) Late on the same day, the JTWC issued their final advisory on Mawar, as it was deeply embedded in the [baroclinic zone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baroclinic_zone "Baroclinic zone") and its low-level circulation center had decoupled behind its convection.[[85]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-86) On June 6, Mawar fully became an extratropical cyclone, and the JMA issued their final advisory on the system.[[86]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-87) The system was last noted east of the [Kamchatka Peninsula](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kamchatka_Peninsula "Kamchatka Peninsula") on June 13.[[87]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-88)

Mawar brought torrential rain to parts of the Philippines including the Bicol Region while enhancing the southwest monsoon which triggered delays and cancelled of air flights. In Bicol region, more than 332 passengers were stranded at ports due to Mawar.[[88]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-89) Different domestic and international flights were forced to divert at [Clark Air Base](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clark_Air_Base "Clark Air Base") rather than [NAIA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ninoy_Aquino_International_Airport "Ninoy Aquino International Airport") due to bad weather. Some other flights were also cancelled.[[89]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-90)[[90]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-91) At least three were reported dead due to rains brought by Mawar.[[91]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-ndrrmc.gov.ph-92)

### Typhoon Guchol (Butchoy)

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=8 "Edit section: Typhoon Guchol (Butchoy)")]

Very strong typhoon(JMA)
Category 4 super typhoon(SSHWS)
[![Image 15](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Guchol_Jun_17_2012_0230Z.jpg/250px-Guchol_Jun_17_2012_0230Z.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Guchol_Jun_17_2012_0230Z.jpg)[![Image 16](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Guchol_2012_track.png/250px-Guchol_2012_track.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Guchol_2012_track.png)
Duration June 10– June 19
Peak intensity 185 km/h (115 mph) (10-min);

930[hPa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit) "Pascal (unit)")([mbar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(unit) "Bar (unit)"))

Main article: [Typhoon Guchol (2012)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Guchol_(2012) "Typhoon Guchol (2012)")

Late on June 7, a tropical disturbance formed south-southeast of [Pohnpei](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pohnpei "Pohnpei").[[92]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-93) By the next day, the [Joint Typhoon Warning Center (JTWC)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center "Joint Typhoon Warning Center") issued a [Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_Cyclone_Formation_Alert "Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert") on the system, but cancelled it late on June 9.[[93]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-94)[[94]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-95) The JMA upgraded the low-pressure area to a tropical depression early on June 11, with the JTWC subsequently following suit.[[95]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-96)[[96]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-97) Early on the next day, the JTWC upgraded the system to a tropical storm, and later the JMA also upgraded it to a tropical storm and named it _Guchol_.[[97]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-98)[[98]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-99) Early on June 14, the JMA upgraded Guchol to a severe tropical storm, and the PAGASA assigned the local name _Butchoy_ on the system as it entered the Philippine Area of Responsibility.[[99]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-100)[[100]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-101) Later that day, the JTWC upgraded Guchol to a category 1 typhoon, as [convection](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atmospheric_convection "Atmospheric convection") started to organize.[[101]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-102) It continued to intensify into a category 2 typhoon on June 15, as it became better organized and started to develop more convection.[[102]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-103) As Guchol went through [rapid intensification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rapid_intensification "Rapid intensification") with a well defined [eye](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eye_(cyclone) "Eye (cyclone)") on June 16, the JMA upgraded it to a typhoon early that day, and the JTWC upgraded it further to a category 3 typhoon, and later a category 4 super typhoon.[[103]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-104)[[104]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-105)[[105]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-106) Guchol reached peak intensity late on June 17,[[106]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-107) before it began to undergo an [eyewall replacement cycle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eyewall_replacement_cycle "Eyewall replacement cycle") as the storm weakened under moderate vertical wind shear on June 18,[[107]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-108) and later started its [extratropical transition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extratropical_transition "Extratropical transition"). The JTWC downgraded Guchol to a tropical storm on June 19, as it made landfall over [Kii Peninsula](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kii_Peninsula "Kii Peninsula") in Japan.[[108]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-109) Later that day, the JMA downgraded Guchol to a severe tropical storm, as it traversed Japan.[[109]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-110) On June 20, the JMA issued their last advisories on Guchol, as it fully transitioned into an extratropical cyclone northeast of Japan.[[110]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-111)

Between June 14 and 18, Guchol enhanced the southwestern monsoon over the Philippines, resulting in widespread rains. However, the effects of these rains were limited and only one fatality took place.[[111]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-GucholNDRRMCfinal-112) In Japan, airlines cancelled 420 domestic and international flights because of the strong winds, affecting 32,600 passengers. The town of [Nachikatsuura](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nachikatsuura,_Wakayama "Nachikatsuura, Wakayama"), some 400 kilometres southwest of Tokyo, ordered nearly 1,600 residents to evacuate, warning of the danger of landslides brought on by heavy rain, media reports said. At least two people were killed and eighty others were injured across the country. Total economic losses were estimated in excess of [¥](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japanese_yen "Japanese yen")8 billion (US$100 million).[[112]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-JuneRecap-113)

### Severe Tropical Storm Talim (Carina)

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=9 "Edit section: Severe Tropical Storm Talim (Carina)")]

Severe tropical storm(JMA)
Tropical storm(SSHWS)
[![Image 17](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Talim_Jun_19_2012_0525Z.jpg/250px-Talim_Jun_19_2012_0525Z.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Talim_Jun_19_2012_0525Z.jpg)[![Image 18](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Talim_2012_track.png/250px-Talim_2012_track.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Talim_2012_track.png)
Duration June 16– June 20
Peak intensity 95 km/h (60 mph) (10-min);

985[hPa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit) "Pascal (unit)")([mbar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(unit) "Bar (unit)"))

On June 16, the JMA started to issue advisories on a tropical depression, located to the east of [Hainan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hainan "Hainan"), [China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China "China").[[113]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-114) By the next day, the JTWC issued a TCFA on the system, as deep convection was consolidating to its low-level circulation center.[[114]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-115) The JMA later upgraded the system to a tropical storm, naming it _Talim_.[[115]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-116) The JTWC subsequently started to issue advisories on Talim, as convection was quickly developing northward into the center.[[116]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-117) On June 18, the JTWC upgraded Talim to a tropical storm, as a [scatterometer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scatterometer "Scatterometer") pass supported gale-force winds on the southern periphery of the system.[[117]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-118) However, as it moved east-northeastward, moderate to strong wind shear caused its deep convection to be displaced to the south, leaving its center partially exposed.[[118]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-119) By the next day, the system's center became fully exposed due to the continued effects of high wind shear.[[119]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-120) Despite that, Talim strengthened into a severe tropical storm.[[120]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-121) On June 20, the JMA downgraded Talim to a tropical storm, as the system tracked towards the [Taiwan Strait](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taiwan_Strait "Taiwan Strait").[[121]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-122)[[122]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-123) The PAGASA later assigned the local name _Carina_ on the system, as it entered the Philippine Area of Responsibility.[[123]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-124) Late on June 20, both the JMA and the JTWC downgraded Talim to a tropical depression, as land interaction significantly weakened the system's organization.[[124]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-125)[[125]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-126) The JTWC issued their final advisory on the system by the next day.[[126]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-127)

In Hong Kong, the Strong Wind Signal No.3 was raised as Talim moved near the territory. Many fallen trees were reported, along with a yacht that ran aground due to its anchor being broken.[[127]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-128) Throughout China, 1 person was killed and total economic losses were counted to be [CNY](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_yuan "Chinese yuan")2.25 billion (US$354 million).[[128]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-China_Member_Report-129)

### Tropical Storm Doksuri (Dindo)

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=10 "Edit section: Tropical Storm Doksuri (Dindo)")]

Tropical storm(JMA)
Tropical storm(SSHWS)
[![Image 19](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Doksuri_Jun_29_2012_0605Z.jpg/250px-Doksuri_Jun_29_2012_0605Z.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Doksuri_Jun_29_2012_0605Z.jpg)[![Image 20](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Doksuri_2012_track.png/250px-Doksuri_2012_track.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Doksuri_2012_track.png)
Duration June 25– June 30
Peak intensity 75 km/h (45 mph) (10-min);

992[hPa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit) "Pascal (unit)")([mbar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(unit) "Bar (unit)"))

On June 25, the JMA started to monitor a tropical depression that had developed, within the monsoon trough about 1,585 km (985 mi) to the southeast of Manila, Philippines.[[129]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-130)[[130]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-131) During that day the depression moved north-westwards and consolidated further before during the next day, PAGASA started to monitor it as Tropical Depression Dindo.[[131]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-132)[[132]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-133) Later that day, the JMA upgraded the system to a tropical storm and named it Doksuri,[[133]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-134) and the JTWC upgraded Doksuri to a tropical depression.[[134]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-135) Late on the same day, the JTWC upgraded Doksuri to a tropical storm.[[135]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-136) On June 27, Doksuri's low-level circulation center became exposed due to moderate easterly wind shear.[[136]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-137) On June 28, the JTWC downgraded Doksuri to a tropical depression, as the system's exposed circulation center began to undergo an unusual circulation center replacement cycle, which involves a circulation center to be replaced by another new circulation center.[[137]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-138) Late on June 29, Doksuri made landfall over [Nanshui](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Nanshui&action=edit&redlink=1 "Nanshui (page does not exist)"), [Zhuhai](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zhuhai "Zhuhai"), [Guangdong](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guangdong "Guangdong"), China.[[138]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-139) During June 30, the JMA reported that Doksuri had weakened into a tropical depression, before reporting that the depression had dissipated later that day.[[139]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-140) In Macau, the storm caused minor roof damage.[[140]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-HKO_%E2%80%94_Doksuri-141)

### Severe Tropical Storm Khanun (Enteng)

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=11 "Edit section: Severe Tropical Storm Khanun (Enteng)")]

Severe tropical storm(JMA)
Tropical storm(SSHWS)
[![Image 21](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Khanun_at_peak_intensity_Jul_18_2012.jpg/250px-Khanun_at_peak_intensity_Jul_18_2012.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Khanun_at_peak_intensity_Jul_18_2012.jpg)[![Image 22](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Khanun_2012_track.png/250px-Khanun_2012_track.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Khanun_2012_track.png)
Duration July 14– July 19
Peak intensity 95 km/h (60 mph) (10-min);

985[hPa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit) "Pascal (unit)")([mbar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(unit) "Bar (unit)"))

Main article: [Tropical Storm Khanun (2012)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Khanun_(2012) "Tropical Storm Khanun (2012)")

See also: [2012 North Korean floods](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_North_Korean_floods "2012 North Korean floods")

On July 14, the JTWC reported that a tropical disturbance had formed to the north-northeast of Guam.[[141]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-142) As the low's convection started to organize, the JMA to upgraded the system to a tropical depression late on the same day.[[142]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-143)[[143]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-144) Early on the next day, the JTWC issued a TCFA on the system, and it upgraded the system to a tropical depression later that day.[[144]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-145)[[145]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-146) On July 16, the JMA upgraded the system to a tropical storm and named it _Khanun_.[[146]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-147) Later on the same day, the JTWC upgraded Khanun to a tropical storm; also, the PAGASA named it _Enteng_ as the system briefly passed the corner of the Philippine Area of Responsibility.[[147]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-148)[[148]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-149) Late on July 17, the JMA upgraded Khanun to a severe tropical storm.[[149]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-150) On July 18, the JMA downgraded Khanun to a tropical storm, before the system passed over [Jeju](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeju_Province "Jeju Province").[[150]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-151) Khanun weakened into a tropical depression near the [Korean Demilitarized Zone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Korean_Demilitarized_Zone "Korean Demilitarized Zone") early on July 19,[[151]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-152)[[152]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-153) and it became post-tropical late on the same day.[[153]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-154)

The storm killed at least one person in South Korea,[[154]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-155) while in North Korea, state-run media reported that at least seven people were killed in [Kangwon Province](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kangwon_Province_(North_Korea) "Kangwon Province (North Korea)"), with an eighth fatality reported elsewhere. It said the storm caused significant damage, destroying 650 dwelling houses, 30 public buildings, railways, roads, bridges, and various systems. The flooding also inundated nearly 3,870 homes, leaving more than 16,250 people homeless.[[155]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-bnonews2012-156) On July 29, the North Korean government dramatically raised the death toll in the country to 88, with an additional 134 injured. The biggest loss of human life was in two counties of [South Pyongan Province](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Pyongan_Province "South Pyongan Province"). At least 63,000 were made homeless by the flooding, while more than 30,000 hectares of land for growing crops were submerged and will add to growing fears of another looming famine in the country. Three hundred public buildings and 60 factories were damaged during the storm.[[156]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-Al_Jazeera-157)

### Typhoon Vicente (Ferdie)

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=12 "Edit section: Typhoon Vicente (Ferdie)")]

Typhoon(JMA)
Category 4 typhoon(SSHWS)
[![Image 23](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Vicente_2012-07-23_1432Z.jpg/250px-Vicente_2012-07-23_1432Z.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Vicente_2012-07-23_1432Z.jpg)[![Image 24](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Vicente_2012_track.png/250px-Vicente_2012_track.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Vicente_2012_track.png)
Duration July 18– July 25
Peak intensity 150 km/h (90 mph) (10-min);

950[hPa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit) "Pascal (unit)")([mbar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(unit) "Bar (unit)"))

Main article: [Typhoon Vicente](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Vicente "Typhoon Vicente")

Originally [Khanun](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Khanun_(2012) "Tropical Storm Khanun (2012)")'s large area of convention on July 16, the [JMA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency "Japan Meteorological Agency") upgraded the system to a tropical depression on July 18.[[157]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-158) On July 20, the [JTWC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center "Joint Typhoon Warning Center") issued a [TCFA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_Cyclone_Formation_Alert "Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert") on the system;[[158]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-159) soon, the [PAGASA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration "Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration") upgraded it to a tropical depression and named it _Ferdie_.[[159]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-160) The JTWC also upgraded the system to a tropical depression late on the same day.[[160]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-161) After the system moved into the [South China Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_China_Sea "South China Sea") on July 21, the JMA upgraded the system to a tropical storm and named it _Vicente_,[[161]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-162) so did the JTWC.[[162]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-163)

On July 23, due to weak vertical [wind shear](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wind_shear "Wind shear") and high [sea surface temperature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sea_surface_temperature "Sea surface temperature"), Vicente started to undergo an [explosive intensification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rapid_deepening#Explosive_intensification "Rapid deepening") prompting the JMA to upgrade Vicente to a typhoon, and the JTWC upgraded Vicente to a category 4 typhoon later.[[163]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-164) At 16:45 [UTC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time "Coordinated Universal Time"), the [HKO](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hong_Kong_Observatory "Hong Kong Observatory") issued the [Hurricane Signal, No. 10](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hong_Kong_tropical_cyclone_warning_signals "Hong Kong tropical cyclone warning signals"), the first since [Typhoon York](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1999_Pacific_typhoon_season#Typhoon_York_(Neneng) "1999 Pacific typhoon season") in 1999.[[164]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-165) Later, Typhoon Vicente made landfall over [Taishan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taishan,_Guangdong "Taishan, Guangdong") in [Guangdong](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guangdong "Guangdong"), China.[[165]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-166) Due to land interaction, the JMA downgraded Vicente to a severe tropical storm early on July 24, and the JTWC downgraded Vicente to a category 3 typhoon.[[166]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-167)[[167]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-168) Late on the same day, the JMA downgraded Vicente to a tropical depression.[[168]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-169)

### Typhoon Saola (Gener)

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=13 "Edit section: Typhoon Saola (Gener)")]

Typhoon(JMA)
Category 2 typhoon(SSHWS)
[![Image 25](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/TY_Saola_10w_Aug_01_2012.jpg/250px-TY_Saola_10w_Aug_01_2012.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:TY_Saola_10w_Aug_01_2012.jpg)[![Image 26](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Saola_2012_track.png/250px-Saola_2012_track.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Saola_2012_track.png)
Duration July 26– August 5
Peak intensity 130 km/h (80 mph) (10-min);

960[hPa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit) "Pascal (unit)")([mbar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(unit) "Bar (unit)"))

Main article: [Typhoon Saola (2012)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Saola_(2012) "Typhoon Saola (2012)")

On July 26, the JMA reported that a tropical depression had developed within an area of strong vertical windshear in the monsoon trough about 1,000 kilometres (620 mi) to the southeast of Manila in the Philippines.[[169]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-170)[[170]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-171) Early on July 28, the JTWC upgraded the system to a tropical depression, whilst the JMA upgraded it to a tropical storm and named it _Saola_.[[171]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-172)[[172]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-173) Soon, the PAGASA upgraded the system to a tropical depression and named it _Gener_.[[173]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-174) Later that day, the JTWC upgraded Saola to a tropical storm.[[174]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-175) Early on July 29, the JMA upgraded Saola to a severe tropical storm.[[175]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-176) On July 30, the JTWC upgraded Saola to a category 1 typhoon, as it started to develop an eye-like feature,[[176]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-177) but soon downgraded it to a tropical storm late on the same day.[[177]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-178) By the next day, the JTWC reupgraded Saola to a Category 1 typhoon.[[178]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-179) Late on the same day, the JMA upgraded Saola to a typhoon.[[179]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-180) It continued to intensify the next day, reaching its peak intensity as a Category 2 typhoon.[[180]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-181)

Most forecast models predicted Saola to pass near the northern coastline of Taiwan,[[181]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-182) but this is defied on August 1, when Saola had made landfall on Taiwan as a Category 2 typhoon. It moved slowly inland, making a counter-clockwise loop.[[182]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-183)[[183]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-184) As it emerged to the ocean, it weakened to a severe tropical storm on August 2.[[184]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-185) Saola then returned to its northwest track and traversed Taiwan, as it weakened to a tropical storm, before emerging to the [Taiwan Strait](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taiwan_Strait "Taiwan Strait") and approached China.[[185]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-186)[[186]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-187) On August 3, it made its final landfall in China as a tropical storm, with the JTWC issuing their final advisory.[[187]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-188) The JMA later followed suit, as Saola weakened to a tropical depression over [Jiangxi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jiangxi "Jiangxi").[[188]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-189)

### Typhoon Damrey

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=14 "Edit section: Typhoon Damrey")]

Typhoon(JMA)
Category 1 typhoon(SSHWS)
[![Image 27](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Damrey_2012-08-02_0245Z.jpg/250px-Damrey_2012-08-02_0245Z.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Damrey_2012-08-02_0245Z.jpg)[![Image 28](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Damrey_2012_track.png/250px-Damrey_2012_track.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Damrey_2012_track.png)
Duration July 27– August 4
Peak intensity 130 km/h (80 mph) (10-min);

965[hPa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit) "Pascal (unit)")([mbar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(unit) "Bar (unit)"))

Main article: [Typhoon Damrey (2012)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Damrey_(2012) "Typhoon Damrey (2012)")

Originally a [cold-core low](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold-core_low "Cold-core low"), the system became a tropical disturbance southwest of [Minamitorishima](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minamitorishima "Minamitorishima") late on July 26. Early on July 27, the [Japan Meteorological Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency "Japan Meteorological Agency") (JMA) upgraded it to a tropical depression.[[189]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-190) On July 28, the [Joint Typhoon Warning Center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center "Joint Typhoon Warning Center") (JTWC) issued a [Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_Cyclone_Formation_Alert "Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert") on the system, before the JMA upgraded it to a tropical storm and named it _Damrey_.[[190]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-191)[[191]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-192) Late on the same day, the JTWC upgraded Damrey to a tropical depression, and even upgraded it to a tropical storm on the next day.[[192]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-193)[[193]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-194) After Damrey had drifted slowly for two days, the JMA upgraded it to a severe tropical storm northeast of [Chichi-jima](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chichi-jima "Chichi-jima") late on July 30, when the storm began to accelerate moving west-northwest and form a banding eye.[[194]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-195) On August 1, the JTWC upgraded Damrey to a category 1 typhoon, while the system passed through the [Ōsumi Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C5%8Csumi_Islands "Ōsumi Islands") in Japan, as it started to develop a well defined eye.[[195]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-196) When Damrey drifted towards [Yellow Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yellow_Sea "Yellow Sea") on August 2, the JMA upgraded it to a typhoon.[[196]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-197) Soon, Typhoon Damrey made landfall over [Xiangshui County](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xiangshui_County "Xiangshui County") in [Jiangsu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jiangsu "Jiangsu"), China at 13:30 [UTC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time "Coordinated Universal Time") (21:30 [CST](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Time_in_China#People's_Republic_of_China "Time in China")).[[197]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-198) Late on August 2, the JTWC downgraded Damrey to a tropical storm with a final warning,[[198]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-199) with the JMA downgrading it to a severe tropical storm.[[199]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-200) By August 3, the JMA downgraded Damrey to a tropical depression when it was located in [Shandong](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shandong "Shandong").[[200]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-201) The system then dissipated near [Hebei](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebei "Hebei") on August 4.[[201]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-202)

### Typhoon Haikui

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=15 "Edit section: Typhoon Haikui")]

Main article: [Typhoon Haikui (2012)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Haikui_(2012) "Typhoon Haikui (2012)")

Typhoon(JMA)
Category 1 typhoon(SSHWS)
[![Image 29](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Haikui_Aug_6_2012_0220Z.jpg/250px-Haikui_Aug_6_2012_0220Z.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Haikui_Aug_6_2012_0220Z.jpg)[![Image 30](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Haikui_2012_track.png/250px-Haikui_2012_track.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Haikui_2012_track.png)
Duration August 1– August 11
Peak intensity 120 km/h (75 mph) (10-min);

965[hPa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit) "Pascal (unit)")([mbar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(unit) "Bar (unit)"))

Main article: [Typhoon Haikui (2012)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Haikui_(2012) "Typhoon Haikui (2012)")

Late on July 31, a tropical disturbance formed within a large [monsoon trough](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monsoon_trough "Monsoon trough"). On August 1, the [Japan Meteorological Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency "Japan Meteorological Agency") (JMA) mentioned the system as a tropical depression southeast of [Iwo Jima](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iwo_Jima "Iwo Jima"), and the [Joint Typhoon Warning Center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center "Joint Typhoon Warning Center") (JTWC) issued a [Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_Cyclone_Formation_Alert "Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert") late on the same day.[[202]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-203)[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-204) Late on August 2, the JTWC upgraded it to a tropical depression, before the JMA upgraded the system to a tropical storm and named it _Haikui_ early on the next day.[[204]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-205)[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-206) Early on August 4, the JTWC upgraded Haikui to a tropical storm.[[206]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-207) On August 5, the JMA upgraded Haikui to a severe tropical storm when it was located north-northeast of [Kume Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kume_Island "Kume Island").[[207]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-208) The JTWC upgraded Haikui to a category 1 typhoon late on August 6, as it developed an eye.[[208]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-209) At 12:00 UTC on August 7, the JMA upgraded Haikui to a typhoon.[[209]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-210) Later, Typhoon Haikui made landfall over [Xiangshan County](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xiangshan_County,_Zhejiang "Xiangshan County, Zhejiang") in [Zhejiang](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zhejiang "Zhejiang"), China at 19:20 [UTC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time "Coordinated Universal Time") (03:20 [CST](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China_time "China time") on August 8).[[210]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-211) Early on August 8, the JMA downgraded Haikui to a severe tropical storm, when the JTWC issued the final warning.[[211]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-212)[[212]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-213) Soon, the JMA downgraded Haikui to a tropical storm.[[213]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-214) Haikui further weakened to a tropical depression on August 9, with the JMA issuing their last advisory on the system.[[214]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-215)

### Severe Tropical Storm Kirogi

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=16 "Edit section: Severe Tropical Storm Kirogi")]

Severe tropical storm(JMA)
Tropical storm(SSHWS)
[![Image 31](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Kirogi_Aug_9_2012.jpg/250px-Kirogi_Aug_9_2012.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Kirogi_Aug_9_2012.jpg)[![Image 32](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Kirogi_2012_track.png/250px-Kirogi_2012_track.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Kirogi_2012_track.png)
Duration August 3– August 10
Peak intensity 95 km/h (60 mph) (10-min);

990[hPa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit) "Pascal (unit)")([mbar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(unit) "Bar (unit)"))

During August 3, the JMA reported that a tropical depression had developed, about 720 km (445 mi) to the northwest of Wake Island.[[215]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-Kirogi_BT-216) Over the next day the system gradually developed further, before the JTWC started to monitor the system as Tropical Depression 13W, late on August 4.[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-Prog_1-217)[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-13W_BT-218)

On August 5, the JTWC upgraded the system to a tropical storm.[[218]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-219) Early on August 6, the JMA reported that the system had become extratropical.[[219]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-220) However, the JMA designated it as a tropical storm with the name _Kirogi_ early on August 8.[[220]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-221) Early on August 9, the JTWC downgraded Kirogi to a tropical depression.[[221]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-222) Later, the JMA upgraded Kirogi to a severe tropical storm, it reached its peak intensity,[[222]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-223) while the JTWC upgraded it to a tropical storm again.[[223]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-224) Later that day, the JTWC issued its final warning on Kirogi as it transitioned from a warm cored tropical system to a cold cored subtropical system.[[224]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-225) The remnants of the system then entered the [Sea of Okhotsk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sea_of_Okhotsk "Sea of Okhotsk").[[225]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-226)

### Typhoon Kai-tak (Helen)

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=17 "Edit section: Typhoon Kai-tak (Helen)")]

Typhoon(JMA)
Category 1 typhoon(SSHWS)
[![Image 33](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Kai-tak_Aug_17_2012.jpg/250px-Kai-tak_Aug_17_2012.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Kai-tak_Aug_17_2012.jpg)[![Image 34](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Kai-tak_2012_track.png/250px-Kai-tak_2012_track.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Kai-tak_2012_track.png)
Duration August 12– August 18
Peak intensity 120 km/h (75 mph) (10-min);

970[hPa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit) "Pascal (unit)")([mbar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(unit) "Bar (unit)"))

Main article: [Typhoon Kai-tak (2012)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Kai-tak_(2012) "Typhoon Kai-tak (2012)")

The monsoonal trough spawned a tropical disturbance early on August 10,[[226]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-227) which had organizing convection and a weak circulation.[[227]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-228) Early on August 12, the [Japan Meteorological Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency "Japan Meteorological Agency") (JMA) started tracking the system as a weak Tropical Depression with winds under 30 knots.[[228]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-229)[Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration "Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration") (PAGASA) started issuing advisories on the system, naming it _Helen_.[[229]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-230) That day, the JTWC also initiated advisories on Tropical Depression 14W.[[230]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-231) Early on August 13, the JMA upgraded the depression to Tropical Storm Kai-tak (_1213_).[[231]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-232) and 9 hours later the JTWC followed suit.[[232]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-233) Later the same day, the JMA upgraded it to a Severe Tropical Storm.[[233]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-234) On August 15, the convection increased as outflow improved, and the JTWC upgraded Kai-tak to a typhoon.[[234]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-235) The storm continued towards China, with deepening convection due to decreasing wind shear.[[235]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-236) However, it was only at 0000 UTC on August 16 when the JMA officially declared Kai-tak a typhoon.[[236]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-237) At the same time, the PAGASA issued their last warning on Kai-tak, otherwise known as Helen, locally, as it left the Philippine area of Responsibility.[[237]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-238)

On the morning of August 17, Kai-tak made landfall over the [Leizhou peninsula](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leizhou_Peninsula "Leizhou Peninsula") in southern China as a typhoon.[[238]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-239) Within 6 hours, Kai-tak made a second landfall over the northeast coast of Vietnam and weakened slightly to a tropical storm.[[239]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-240) Later that night, the JTWC issued their final warning on the system as it weakened further and sped up inland.[[240]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-241) The JMA stopped tracking the storm early the next morning, no longer considering it a tropical cyclone.[[241]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-242)

### Typhoon Tembin (Igme)

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=18 "Edit section: Typhoon Tembin (Igme)")]

Typhoon(JMA)
Category 4 typhoon(SSHWS)
[![Image 35](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Tembin_Aug_20_2012_0235Z.jpg/250px-Tembin_Aug_20_2012_0235Z.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Tembin_Aug_20_2012_0235Z.jpg)[![Image 36](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Tembin_2012_track.png/250px-Tembin_2012_track.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Tembin_2012_track.png)
Duration August 17– August 30
Peak intensity 150 km/h (90 mph) (10-min);

950[hPa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit) "Pascal (unit)")([mbar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(unit) "Bar (unit)"))

Main article: [Typhoon Tembin (2012)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Tembin_(2012) "Typhoon Tembin (2012)")

On August 16, a tropical disturbance formed southeast of [Taiwan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taiwan "Taiwan").[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-243) On August 17, the JMA mentioned it as a tropical depression, as a [subtropical ridge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subtropical_ridge "Subtropical ridge") pushed the system southwards.[[243]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-244) The JTWC issued a [TCFA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_Cyclone_Formation_Alert "Tropical Cyclone Formation Alert") on the system late on August 18;[[244]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-245) early on the next day, the JMA upgraded it to a tropical storm and named it _Tembin_, and the JTWC upgraded it to a tropical depression.[[245]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-246)[[246]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-247) Soon, the PAGASA also upgraded it to a tropical depression and named it _Igme_.[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-248) On August 20, Tembin entered a period of [explosive intensification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rapid_deepening "Rapid deepening") by excellent dual outflow, prompting both the JMA and the JTWC upgrading it to a typhoon.[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-249)[[249]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-250) By the end of the same day, Tembin reached its initial peak intensity as a Category 4 typhoon,[[250]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-251) before it started to weaken by the next day as a [TUTT](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_upper_tropospheric_trough "Tropical upper tropospheric trough") cell developed over the system.[[251]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-252)

On August 22, Tembin began reintensify, as an eye feature was forming once again.[[252]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-253) By the next day, Tembin re-intensified into a category 3 typhoon,[[253]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-254) before it made landfall over [Pingtung](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pingtung_County "Pingtung County"), [Taiwan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taiwan "Taiwan") later on the same day.[[254]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-255) Due to land interaction, the JMA downgraded Tembin to a severe tropical storm early on August 24,[[255]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-256) and the JTWC downgraded it to a tropical storm later.[[256]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-257) Soon, the JTWC upgraded Tembin to a typhoon when it moved into the [South China Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_China_Sea "South China Sea").[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-258) Late on August 25, the JMA upgraded Tembin to a typhoon again,[[258]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-259) and the system intensified into a category 2 typhoon early on the next day.[[259]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-260) Afterwards, Typhoon Tembin interacted with the nearby [Typhoon Bolaven](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Bolaven_(2012) "Typhoon Bolaven (2012)").[[260]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-261) Over the next few days, Tembin made a counterclockwise loop eastward,[[261]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-262) moving back into the Philippine Area of Responsibility (PAR) in the process, causing more rainfall over in the Philippines.[[262]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-263) Afterwards, the JTWC downgraded the system to a tropical storm late on August 27, as it turned north-northeastward.[[263]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-264) The JMA soon downgraded it to a severe tropical storm by the next day.[[264]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-265) On August 30, Tembin made landfall on [South Korea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Korea "South
