Korea"),[[265]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-266)[[266]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-267) and transitioned into an extratropical storm.[[267]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-268)

### Typhoon Bolaven (Julian)

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=19 "Edit section: Typhoon Bolaven (Julian)")]

Very strong typhoon(JMA)
Category 4 typhoon(SSHWS)
[![Image 37](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Bolaven_2012-08-25_0420Z_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Bolaven_2012-08-25_0420Z_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bolaven_2012-08-25_0420Z_(cropped).jpg)[![Image 38](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Bolaven_2012_track.png/250px-Bolaven_2012_track.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bolaven_2012_track.png)
Duration August 19– August 29
Peak intensity 185 km/h (115 mph) (10-min);

910[hPa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit) "Pascal (unit)")([mbar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(unit) "Bar (unit)"))

Main article: [Typhoon Bolaven (2012)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Bolaven_(2012) "Typhoon Bolaven (2012)")

Forming as a tropical depression on August 19 to the southwest of the [Mariana Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mariana_Islands "Mariana Islands"),[[268]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-269) Bolaven steadily intensified as it slowly moved west-northwestward in a region favoring tropical development. The system was soon upgraded to a tropical storm less than a day after formation and further to a typhoon by August 21.[[269]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-270)[[270]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-271) Strengthening became more gradual thereafter as Bolaven grew in size.[[271]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-272) On August 24, the system attained its peak intensity with winds of 185 km/h (115 mph) and a [barometric pressure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barometric_pressure "Barometric pressure") of 910[mbar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(unit) "Bar (unit)") ([hPa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit) "Pascal (unit)"); 26.87[inHg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inches_of_Mercury "Inches of Mercury")). Weakening only slightly, the storm passed directly over [Okinawa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Okinawa_Island "Okinawa Island") on August 26 as it began accelerating toward the north.[[272]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-273)[[273]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-274)[[274]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-275) Steady weakening continued as Bolaven approached the [Korean Peninsula](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Korean_Peninsula "Korean Peninsula") and it eventually made [landfall](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Landfall_(meteorology) "Landfall (meteorology)") in [North Korea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Korea "North Korea") late on August 28 before transitioning into an [extratropical cyclone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone "Extratropical cyclone").[[275]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-276) The remnants rapidly tracked northeastward and was last noted over the [Russian Far East](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Far_East "Russian Far East").[[276]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-277)

Although Bolaven struck the [Ryukyu Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ryukyu_Islands "Ryukyu Islands") as a powerful typhoon, damage was less than expected. Relatively few buildings were damaged or destroyed across the region.[[277]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-278) The most significant effects stemmed from heavy rains, amounting to 551.5 mm (21.71 in), that caused flash flooding and landslides.[[278]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-279) One person drowned on [Amami Ōshima](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amami_%C5%8Cshima "Amami Ōshima") after being swept away by a swollen river.[[279]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-280) In mainland Japan, two people drowned after being swept away by rough seas.[[280]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-281)[[281]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-282) In [South Korea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Korea "South Korea"), 19 people were killed by the storm. Many buildings were damaged and approximately 1.9 million homes were left without power.[[282]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-283)[[283]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-284) Losses in the country reached [₩](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Korean_won "South Korean won")420 billion (US$374.3 million), the majority of which was due to destroyed apple orchards.[[284]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-285) Significant damage also took place in [North Korea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Korea "North Korea") where at least 59 people were killed and 50 others were reported missing.[[285]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-286) Additionally, 6,700 homes were destroyed. Offshore, nine people drowned after two Chinese vessels sank.[[286]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-287) Total economic losses in China were counted to be CNY 19.82 billion (US$3.126 billion).[[128]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-China_Member_Report-129)

### Typhoon Sanba (Karen)

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=20 "Edit section: Typhoon Sanba (Karen)")]

Violent typhoon(JMA)
Category 5 super typhoon(SSHWS)
[![Image 39](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Sanba_2012-09-14_0101Z.jpg/250px-Sanba_2012-09-14_0101Z.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sanba_2012-09-14_0101Z.jpg)[![Image 40](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Sanba_2012_path.png/250px-Sanba_2012_path.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sanba_2012_path.png)
Duration September 10– September 18
Peak intensity 205 km/h (125 mph) (10-min);

900[hPa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit) "Pascal (unit)")([mbar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(unit) "Bar (unit)"))

Main article: [Typhoon Sanba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Sanba "Typhoon Sanba")

A low-pressure area formed east of [Palau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palau "Palau") on September 9.[[287]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-288) On September 10, both the JMA and the JTWC upgraded it to a tropical depression.[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-289)[[289]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-290)[[290]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-291) As the system entered the PAR early on September 11, the PAGASA named it _Karen_.[[291]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-292) At the same time, the JMA upgraded the system to a tropical storm and named it _Sanba_, and the JTWC also upgraded it to a tropical storm later.[[292]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-293) Late on September 12, Sanba began [explosive intensification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rapid_deepening "Rapid deepening"), prompting the JMA upgrading it to a severe tropical storm and even a typhoon later.[[293]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-294)[[294]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-295) On September 13, the JTWC reported that Sanba rapidly strengthened into a category 5 super typhoon, the strongest since [Megi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Megi_(2010) "Typhoon Megi (2010)") in 2010.[[295]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-296) By the next day, the system started to weaken as it had undergone an eyewall replacement cycle.[[296]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-297) It soon ended up with a 57 kilometer-wide eye.[[297]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-298) On September 17, Sanba made landfall over South Korea.[[298]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-299)

In [Kōchi Prefecture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/K%C5%8Dchi_Prefecture "Kōchi Prefecture"), Japan, 222 hectares (548 acres) of agricultural land was damaged by the storm, with losses reaching [¥](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japanese_yen "Japanese yen")50 million (US$640 thousand).[[299]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-300) Throughout Okinawa, damage to agriculture, forestry, and fisheries amounted to ¥900 million (US$11.5 million).[[300]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-301)

### Typhoon Jelawat (Lawin)

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=21 "Edit section: Typhoon Jelawat (Lawin)")]

Violent typhoon(JMA)
Category 5 super typhoon(SSHWS)
[![Image 41](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Jelawat_2012-09-25_0210Z.jpg/250px-Jelawat_2012-09-25_0210Z.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Jelawat_2012-09-25_0210Z.jpg)[![Image 42](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Jelawat_2012_track.png/250px-Jelawat_2012_track.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Jelawat_2012_track.png)
Duration September 20– October 1
Peak intensity 205 km/h (125 mph) (10-min);

905[hPa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit) "Pascal (unit)")([mbar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(unit) "Bar (unit)"))

Main article: [Typhoon Jelawat (2012)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Jelawat_(2012) "Typhoon Jelawat (2012)")

On September 18, a tropical disturbance formed to the east of [Guam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guam "Guam").[[301]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-302) Late on the next day, the JTWC issued a TCFA on the system.[[302]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-303) By September 20, both the JMA and the PAGASA upgraded the low-pressure area to a tropical depression, with the latter naming it as _Lawin_.[[303]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-304)[[304]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-305) The JTWC subsequently followed suit and upgraded it to a tropical depression.[[305]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-306) Late on the same day, the JMA upgraded the system to a tropical storm and named it _Jelawat_, and so did the JTWC.[[306]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-307)[[307]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-308) Half a day later, the JMA upgraded Jelawat to a severe tropical storm.[[308]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-309) Early on September 23, both the JMA and the JTWC upgraded Jelawat to a typhoon.[[309]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-310)[[310]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-311) It started to undergo [explosive intensification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rapid_deepening "Rapid deepening"), becoming a category 4 typhoon in 12 hours, as it developed a small eye.[[311]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-312) Late on September 24, as Jelawat developed a 19-kilometre-wide (12 mi) eye, the JTWC upgraded the system to a category 5-equivalent super typhoon.[[312]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-313) By the next day, the system started its eyewall replacement cycle.[[313]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-314) By September 26, it weakened to a Category 4 super typhoon as it completed the cycle,[[314]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-315) with its eye becoming 74 kilometers across by the next day.[[315]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-316) On September 28, it started another eyewall replacement cycle.[[316]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-317) This led to the system weakening to a category 3-equivalent typhoon,[[317]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-318) and a category 2-equivalent system on the next day due to cooling sea surface temperatures.[[318]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-319) It further weakened to a category 1-equivalent typhoon late on the same day.[[319]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-320) On September 30, the JTWC downgraded Jelawat to a tropical storm,[[320]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-321) before it made landfall on Japan a few hours later.[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-322) The JMA downgraded Jelawat to a severe tropical storm late on the same day, with the JTWC issuing its final advisory.[[322]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-323)[[323]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-324) The JMA further downgraded the system to a tropical storm by the next day,[[324]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-325) before it fully became an extratropical cyclone six hours later.[[325]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-326)

### Severe Tropical Storm Ewiniar

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=22 "Edit section: Severe Tropical Storm Ewiniar")]

Severe tropical storm(JMA)
Tropical storm(SSHWS)
[![Image 43](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Ewiniar_Sept_27_2012_0325Z.jpg/250px-Ewiniar_Sept_27_2012_0325Z.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Ewiniar_Sept_27_2012_0325Z.jpg)[![Image 44](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Ewiniar_2012_track.png/250px-Ewiniar_2012_track.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Ewiniar_2012_track.png)
Duration September 23– September 30
Peak intensity 95 km/h (60 mph) (10-min);

985[hPa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit) "Pascal (unit)")([mbar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(unit) "Bar (unit)"))

On September 22, the JTWC reported that a low-pressure area was developing to the west of Guam, around 650 nautical miles (1,200 km) east-northeast of Typhoon Jelawat.[[326]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-327) By the next day, the JMA upgraded it to a tropical depression.[[327]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-328) On September 24, the JTWC upgraded the system to a tropical depression, although deep convection was displaced to the south due to moderate vertical wind shear associated with Jelawat, leaving its low-level circulation center exposed.[[328]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-329)[[329]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-330) The center then began to consolidate, with deep convection wrapping over its eastern quadrant, prompting both the JMA and the JTWC to upgrade the system to a tropical storm, with the former naming it as _Ewiniar_.[[330]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-331)[[331]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-332)

Moving north-northeastward along the periphery of the subtropical ridge, Ewiniar's center continued to be displaced from the main convection due to moderate wind shear.[[332]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-333) By September 26, Ewiniar struggled to maintain its deep convection due to the continued effects of wind shear.[[333]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-334) Despite that, the JMA upgraded Ewiniar into a severe tropical storm.[[334]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-335) On the next day, the system reached peak intensity as it turned northward, with weakening convection wrapping to its center,[[335]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-336) before it became embedded within a subtropical trough.[[336]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-337) However, deep convection wrapped the system as it became quasi-stationary late on the same day,[[337]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-338) before returning to a northeastward track soon after.[[338]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-339) By the next day, Ewiniar's center became partially exposed, and it began to weaken.[[339]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-340)[[340]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-341) On September 29, the JMA downgraded the system to a tropical storm, as convection was being displaced to the northeast of its center by strong vertical wind shear.[[341]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-342)[[342]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-343) The JTWC issued their final advisory on the same day, as Ewiniar's center fully separated from its convection, and had undergone extratropical transition.[[343]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-344) Ewiniar then became extratropical by the next day.[[344]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-345)

### Severe Tropical Storm Maliksi

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=23 "Edit section: Severe Tropical Storm Maliksi")]

Severe tropical storm(JMA)
Tropical storm(SSHWS)
[![Image 45](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Maliksi_Oct_03_2012.jpg/250px-Maliksi_Oct_03_2012.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Maliksi_Oct_03_2012.jpg)[![Image 46](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Maliksi_2012_track.png/250px-Maliksi_2012_track.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Maliksi_2012_track.png)
Duration September 29– October 4
Peak intensity 95 km/h (60 mph) (10-min);

985[hPa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit) "Pascal (unit)")([mbar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(unit) "Bar (unit)"))

On September 28, the JTWC started to monitor an area of convection approximately 80 nautical miles (150 km) to the northwest of Chuuk. At the time, it had a broad but slowly developing low-level circulation center, and was under a marginal environment of warm sea surface temperatures, weak vertical wind shear and limited poleward outflow.[[345]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-346) As the system's center began to consolidate,[[346]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-ABPW_0929-347) the JMA upgraded it to a tropical depression by the next day.[[347]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-348) Half a day later, the JTWC issued a TCFA on the system, as its center became better defined, with convection wrapping into it,[[348]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-349) before it subsequently upgraded the system to a tropical depression, designating it as 20W.[[349]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-350) As the system continued to organize itself, the JMA upgraded it to a tropical storm by October 1, naming it as _Maliksi_.[[350]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-351)[[351]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-352) The JTWC subsequently followed suit, although its deep convection to the southeast were yet to wrap towards its center.[[352]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-353)

Moving northwestward under the southwest periphery of the subtropical ridge, Maliksi continued to improve its center by the next day, with convective banding wrapping tightly towards it.[[353]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-354) However, microwave imagery showed the system had become less organized 12 hours later, with its center becoming elongated.[[354]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-355) Nonetheless, the JMA upgraded Maliksi to a severe tropical storm late on the same day, as it began to improve once again.[[355]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-356)[[356]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-357) As it turned to the northeast, deep convection from the system became isolated to the east, due to increasing wind shear and unfavorable conditions as it started transitioning to an extratropical system.[[357]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-358) As a result, the JTWC issued their final advisory on Maliksi late on October 3, as convection became greatly sheared to the northeast.[[358]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-359) The system then became fully extratropical by the next day.[[359]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-360) The extratropical system went on to merge with a front, becoming an intense hurricane-force low on October 5, before reforming near the [Aleutian Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aleutian_Islands "Aleutian Islands") and dissipating near [Alaska](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alaska "Alaska") on October 11.[[360]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-361)

As the system was developing near the Mariana Islands, tropical storm warnings were issued in [Alamagan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alamagan "Alamagan"), [Pagan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pagan "Pagan") and [Agrihan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agrihan "Agrihan") on October 1.[[361]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-362) However, as Maliksi moved northwest, the warnings were cancelled by the next day.[[362]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-363)

### Severe Tropical Storm Gaemi (Marce)

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=24 "Edit section: Severe Tropical Storm Gaemi (Marce)")]

Severe tropical storm(JMA)
Tropical storm(SSHWS)
[![Image 47](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Gaemi_Oct_03_2012_0300Z.jpg/250px-Gaemi_Oct_03_2012_0300Z.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Gaemi_Oct_03_2012_0300Z.jpg)[![Image 48](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Gaemi_2012_track.png/250px-Gaemi_2012_track.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Gaemi_2012_track.png)
Duration September 29– October 7
Peak intensity 95 km/h (60 mph) (10-min);

990[hPa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit) "Pascal (unit)")([mbar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(unit) "Bar (unit)"))

Main article: [Tropical Storm Gaemi (2012)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Gaemi_(2012) "Tropical Storm Gaemi (2012)")

On September 29, the JTWC started to monitor an area of convection, within a monsoon trough, approximately 325 nmi (602 km) to the southeast of [Huế](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hu%E1%BA%BF "Huế"), [Vietnam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vietnam "Vietnam"). At the time, it already had an organizing low-level circulation center, and was within a low to moderate wind shear environment.[[346]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-ABPW_0929-347)[[363]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-364) The JMA soon upgraded it to a tropical depression.[[364]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-365) As the depression became quasi-stationary, deep convection consolidated over its center, prompting the JTWC to issue a TCFA by the next day.[[365]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-366) On October 1, the JMA upgraded the system into a tropical storm, naming it as _Gaemi_.[[366]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-367) At the same time, the JTWC started issuing advisories on Gaemi as a tropical depression,[[367]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-368) before subsequently upgrading it to a tropical storm, as a [scatterometer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scatterometer "Scatterometer") pass indicated gale-force winds within the system.[[368]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-369)

Within a weak steering environment, Gaemi moved southward under the influence of a near-equatorial ridge, as it continued to improve.[[369]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-370) By the next day, Gaemi entered the Philippine Area of Responsibility (PAR) as deep convection continued to wrap the system, with the PAGASA assigning its local name _Marce_.[[370]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-371)[[371]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-372) With a central dense overcast over the system's center,[[372]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-373) the JMA upgraded Gaemi to a severe tropical storm on October 3, as it turned to the west-southwest as a building subtropical ridge to the north took command of the system's steering influence.[[373]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-374)[[374]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-Gaemi_8-375) The JTWC originally anticipated the storm to strengthen into a typhoon under favorable conditions,[[374]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-Gaemi_8-375) however, increasing easterly wind shear sheared the system's convection to the west as it turned east by the next day, with its center becoming fully exposed.[[375]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-376) As a result, the JMA downgraded Gaemi to a tropical storm.[[376]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-377) Returning to a westward track,[[377]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-378) Gaemi remained fully exposed by October 5, and was deteriorating under the continued effects of wind shear.[[378]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-379) Later that same day, it exited the PAR, with the PAGASA issuing their final advisory on the storm.[[379]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-380) Gaemi then slightly reintensified by the next day, with deep convection covering its center but most of the convection remained isolated to its west.[[380]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-381) At 6:00 pm [ICT](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indochina_Time "Indochina Time") (11:00 UTC), it made landfall over [Phú Yên Province](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ph%C3%BA_Y%C3%AAn_Province "Phú Yên Province") in Vietnam.[[381]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-Vietnam-382) The JMA subsequently downgraded Gaemi to a tropical depression,[[382]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-383) with the JTWC issuing their final advisory on the system.[[383]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-384) The remnants then spawned an area of convection that developed into [Depression BOB 01](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_North_Indian_Ocean_cyclone_season#Depression_BOB_01 "2012 North Indian Ocean cyclone season") in the Bay of Bengal.[[384]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-385)

As Gaemi, locally known as Marce, moved near the Philippines, signal #1 warnings were issued in [Bataan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bataan "Bataan") and [Zambales](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zambales "Zambales").[[385]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-386) The storm brought heavy rainfall, resulting in a dike partially collapsing in [Occidental Mindoro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Occidental_Mindoro "Occidental Mindoro") and the evacuation of 5 families. 14 student-mountaineers were rescued after being trapped at Papaya River Base Camp in [Mariveles, Bataan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mariveles,_Bataan "Mariveles, Bataan") due to rains caused by Gaemi.[[386]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-387) A storm surge was reported at [San Antonio, Zambales](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Antonio,_Zambales "San Antonio, Zambales") in October 3, damaging 23 houses, and in [Calintaan, Occidental Mindoro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calintaan,_Occidental_Mindoro "Calintaan, Occidental Mindoro") in October 5, damaging 28 houses. A 59-year old fisherman was found dead along the shore of [Nasugbu, Batangas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nasugbu,_Batangas "Nasugbu, Batangas"), after two motorbancas with 3 fishermen onboard capsized amid big waves and strong winds caused by Gaemi.[[387]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-SitRep_Marce-388) In Vietnam, the storm killed 5 people.[[41]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-VNCHMFReport-42)

### Typhoon Prapiroon (Nina)

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=25 "Edit section: Typhoon Prapiroon (Nina)")]

Very strong typhoon(JMA)
Category 3 typhoon(SSHWS)
[![Image 49](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Prapiroon_Oct_12_2012_0420Z.jpg/250px-Prapiroon_Oct_12_2012_0420Z.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Prapiroon_Oct_12_2012_0420Z.jpg)[![Image 50](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Prapiroon_2012_track.png/250px-Prapiroon_2012_track.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Prapiroon_2012_track.png)
Duration October 5– October 19
Peak intensity 165 km/h (105 mph) (10-min);

940[hPa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit) "Pascal (unit)")([mbar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(unit) "Bar (unit)"))

On October 5, the JMA started to monitor a tropical depression that had developed about 115 km (70 mi) to the northwest of [Hagåtña, Guam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hag%C3%A5t%C3%B1a,_Guam "Hagåtña, Guam").[[388]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-389) At the time, the depression had a consolidating low-level circulation center, and was under an environment of warm sea surface temperatures and marginal vertical wind shear.[[389]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-390) With increased central convection and improving but fragmented banding, the system continued to organize, prompting the JTWC to issue a TCFA late on the next day.[[390]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-391) On October 7, the JMA upgraded the tropical depression to a tropical storm, and named it _Prapiroon_.[[391]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-392) At the same time, the JTWC started issuing advisories on Prapiroon as a tropical depression,[[392]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-393) before subsequently upgrading it to a tropical storm, noting its rapid improvement with deep convective banding wrapping from the southwest to the east of the system's center.[[393]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-394) Early by the next day, Prapiroon intensified to a severe tropical storm, as it continued to improve, with tightly-curved banding over its center, while moving westward along the subtropical ridge.[[394]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-395)[[395]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-396) The PAGASA later assigned the local name _Nina_ as the system entered the Philippine Area of Responsibility (PAR).[[396]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-397)

Late on the same day, the JMA upgraded Prapiroon to a typhoon, as deep convective banding was steadily developing along its southern quadrant.[[397]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-398)[[398]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-399) The JTWC subsequently followed suit by October 9, as an eye feature began to develop on satellite imagery.[[399]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-400) On the next day, Prapiroon further intensified into a category 2-equivalent typhoon.[[400]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-401) As it became quasi-stationary, due to a weak steering environment between the subtropical ridge to the northeast and a near-equatorial ridge to the southeast, Prapiroon developed an 18 nmi (33 km) eye,[[401]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-402) reaching its peak intensity as a category 3-equivalent typhoon late on October 11.[[402]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-IBTRACS_Prapiroon-403) By the next day, Prapiroon weakened to a category 2-equivalent typhoon, as its eye became ragged, along with warming cloud tops, while it was steered to the east-northeast by the near-equatorial ridge.[[402]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-IBTRACS_Prapiroon-403)[[403]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-404) On October 13, it further weakened to a category 1-equivalent typhoon due to [upwelling](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Upwelling "Upwelling"), as it slowed its northeastward movement.[[404]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-405)

Prapiroon continued its slow track, as a subtropical ridge to the east began to take control of its steering environment as the near-equatorial ridge weakened, while its central convection decreased, before soon opening a 15 nmi (28 km) eye by the next day.[[405]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-406)[[406]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-407) On October 15, the system reintensified to its secondary peak intensity, as deep convection wrapped its now-60 nmi (110 km) eye, while becoming quasi-stationary once again, entering a [col](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Col_(meteorology) "Col (meteorology)") area as nearby Severe Tropical Storm Maria tracked around the subtropical ridge.[[407]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-408)[[408]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-409) Prapiroon then started to weaken late on the same day, as deep convection decreased in its northeast quadrant, with warming cloud tops, while turning southwestward.[[409]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-410)[[410]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-411) As a result, the JMA downgraded the system to a severe tropical storm by the next day,[[411]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-412) with the JTWC following suit, due to a dry air intrusion in the system's structure, as it started to recurve westwards.[[412]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-413)[[413]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-414) Prapiroon then returned to a northeastward track, cresting the western periphery of the subtropical ridge, while its center became fully exposed as cold air from the [East China Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_China_Sea "East China Sea") advected into the system.[[414]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-415) The storm later exited the PAR, with the PAGASA issuing their final advisory.[[415]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-416) As it started to accelerate on October 18, its deep convection diminished, while dry air surrounded its center, along with increasing wind shear as an upper-level trough created strong [subsidence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subsidence_(atmosphere) "Subsidence (atmosphere)") along the western side of its center.[[416]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-417) Prapiroon soon became embedded in a [baroclinic zone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baroclinic_zone "Baroclinic zone") of strong wind shear, as the system's structure began to be elongated, with its deep convection unraveling and sheared to the north of its center.[[417]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-418)[[418]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-419) It began its extratropical transition late on the same day, with the JTWC issuing their final advisory early on the next day as cool, dry air penetrated the system's center from the west.[[419]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-420)[[420]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-421) Prapiroon fully transitioned to a extratropical cyclone 12 hours later, as it continued northeastward, before turning north and was last noted near the Aleutian Islands on October 23.[[402]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-IBTRACS_Prapiroon-403)

### Severe Tropical Storm Maria

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=26 "Edit section: Severe Tropical Storm Maria")]

Severe tropical storm(JMA)
Tropical storm(SSHWS)
[![Image 51](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Maria_Oct_16_2012.jpg/250px-Maria_Oct_16_2012.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Maria_Oct_16_2012.jpg)[![Image 52](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Maria_2012_track.png/250px-Maria_2012_track.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Maria_2012_track.png)
Duration October 12– October 20
Peak intensity 95 km/h (60 mph) (10-min);

990[hPa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit) "Pascal (unit)")([mbar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(unit) "Bar (unit)"))

Late on October 12, the JMA started to monitor a tropical depression that had developed about 400 km (250 mi) to the northeast of Guam.[[421]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-Maria_BT-422) At the time, the system's convection was sheared to the southwest of its ill-defined & partially exposed low-level circulation center, and was under a low to moderate wind shear environment.[[422]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-423) As deep convection started to build over its center, the JTWC issued a TCFA early on October 14.[[423]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-424) Six hours later, the JMA upgraded the tropical depression to a tropical storm, naming it as _Maria_.[[421]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-Maria_BT-422)[[424]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-425) At the same time, the JTWC started issuing advisories on Maria as a tropical depression,[[425]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-426) before subsequently upgrading it to a tropical storm, as convection continued to deepen.[[426]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-427)

Moving northwestward along the western periphery of the subtropical ridge, the JMA reported that Maria intensified into a severe tropical storm early by the next day.[[427]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-428)[[428]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-429) However, its deep convection became slightly displaced to the south, due to increasing wind shear.[[429]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-430) It soon wrapped into its center again, as wind shear decreased;[[430]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-431) however, the JMA downgraded Maria to a tropical storm by October 16.[[421]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-Maria_BT-422) Maria then reached peak intensity, with an eye feature seen in microwave imagery.[[431]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-432) This became short-lived, as its deep convection began to be sheared to the east of the system due to increasing westerly flow aloft associated with a subtropical [jet stream](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jet_stream "Jet stream").[[432]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-433) By the next day, Maria's convection became displaced to the northeast of its center due to moderate to strong wind shear, as it accelerated northeastward.[[433]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-434) It soon recovered by early October 18, with centralized convection persisting over its center, but it was being impacted by mid-latitude flow around the subtropical ridge.[[434]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-435) However, 12 hours later, strong wind shear significantly sheared the system, exposing its center.[[435]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-436) By the next day, both the JMA and the JTWC downgraded Maria to a tropical depression, with the former issuing their final advisory, as the system's center was becoming elongated.[[436]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-437)[[437]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-438) The JTWC subsequently issued their final advisory on Maria as well.[[438]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-439) The remnants remained traceable until early on October 20, when the JMA reported that Maria had dissipated.[[421]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-Maria_BT-422)

### Typhoon Son-Tinh (Ofel)

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=27 "Edit section: Typhoon Son-Tinh (Ofel)")]

Very strong typhoon(JMA)
Category 3 typhoon(SSHWS)
[![Image 53](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Son-Tinh_2012-10-27_0614Z.jpg/250px-Son-Tinh_2012-10-27_0614Z.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Son-Tinh_2012-10-27_0614Z.jpg)[![Image 54](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Son-Tinh_2012_track.png/250px-Son-Tinh_2012_track.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Son-Tinh_2012_track.png)
Duration October 21– October 29
Peak intensity 155 km/h (100 mph) (10-min);

945[hPa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit) "Pascal (unit)")([mbar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(unit) "Bar (unit)"))

Main article: [Typhoon Son-Tinh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Son-Tinh "Typhoon Son-Tinh")

On October 21, the JMA started to monitor a tropical depression near Palau.[[439]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-440) By the next day the PAGASA started to monitor the tropical depression and named it _Ofel_.[[440]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-441) Late on October 23, the JMA upgraded the tropical depression to a tropical storm, naming it _Son-Tinh_.[[441]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-442) It subsequently made landfall over [Leyte](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leyte "Leyte") as a tropical storm,[[442]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-443) and traversed the Philippines.[[443]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-444) On October 25, Son-Tinh strengthened into a severe tropical storm.[[444]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-445) Son-Tinh reached typhoon strength on October 27.[[445]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-446) Late on October 27, the system [rapidly strengthened](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rapid_deepening "Rapid deepening") into a category 3 typhoon in just 6 hours, as it developed a ragged eye, but soon developed into a well defined eye.[[446]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-447) After affecting Vietnam and Hainan Island,[[447]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-448) it weakened rapidly, first to a tropical storm,[[448]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-449) and then to a tropical depression, due to land interaction and strong wind shear from the north west.[[449]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-450)

In the Philippines, widespread flooding was reported as rivers burst their banks, in some instances rising as much as 12.8 meters in 24 hours. A cargo ship called the ML Lady RP II, sank with around 1,200 sacks of copra near Zamboanga City at the height of the storm. Strong winds derailed a train in Quezon.[[450]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-451) Throughout the Philippines, 27 people were killed by the storm and damage amounted to [PHP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippine_peso "Philippine peso")155 million (US$3.74 million).[[451]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-NDCC17-452)

### Tropical Depression 25W

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=28 "Edit section: Tropical Depression 25W")]

Tropical depression(JMA)
Tropical depression(SSHWS)
[![Image 55](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Tropical_Depression_25W_Nov_14_2012.jpg/250px-Tropical_Depression_25W_Nov_14_2012.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Tropical_Depression_25W_Nov_14_2012.jpg)[![Image 56](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/25W_2012_track.png/250px-25W_2012_track.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:25W_2012_track.png)
Duration November 12– November 15
Peak intensity 55 km/h (35 mph) (10-min);

1004[hPa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit) "Pascal (unit)")([mbar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(unit) "Bar (unit)"))

Early on November 12, the JTWC reported that a tropical disturbance had developed within an area of weak to moderate vertical windshear, about 315 km (195 mi) to the southeast of Manila in the Philippines.[[452]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-25W_BT-453)[[453]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-454) Later that day as the system moved towards the north-northwest, the JTWC reported that the disturbance had become a tropical depression before the JMA followed suit early on November 13.[[452]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-25W_BT-453)[[454]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-455)

### Typhoon Bopha (Pablo)

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=29 "Edit section: Typhoon Bopha (Pablo)")]

Very strong typhoon(JMA)
Category 5 super typhoon(SSHWS)
[![Image 57](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Bopha_2012-12-03_1712Z_%28colored%29.jpg/250px-Bopha_2012-12-03_1712Z_%28colored%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bopha_2012-12-03_1712Z_(colored).jpg)[![Image 58](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Bopha_2012_path.png/250px-Bopha_2012_path.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bopha_2012_path.png)
Duration November 25– December 9
Peak intensity 185 km/h (115 mph) (10-min);

910[hPa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit) "Pascal (unit)")([mbar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(unit) "Bar (unit)"))

Main article: [Typhoon Bopha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Bopha "Typhoon Bopha")

See also: [Effects of Typhoon Bopha in the Caroline Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Effects_of_Typhoon_Bopha_in_the_Caroline_Islands "Effects of Typhoon Bopha in the Caroline Islands")

On November 23, the JTWC reported that a large area of convection persisted 350 nautical miles (650 km; 400 mi) south of [Pohnpei](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pohnpei "Pohnpei") in the [Caroline Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caroline_Islands "Caroline Islands").[[455]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-456) Its organization steadily improved over the next few days under a favorable conditions with warm sea surface temperatures.[[456]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-457) and on November 25 both JTWC and JMA upgraded its status to a Tropical Depression, while the JTWC designated it with _26W_.[[457]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-458)[[458]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-459) During the early hours of November 26, an upper-level anticyclone formed over the center with near-radial outflow and weak vertical wind shear.[[459]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-JTWC_PROG_002-460) Under its influence, 26W strengthened gradually and acquired tropical storm status by that evening. As a result, the JMA officially named the storm _Bopha_.[[460]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-461) On November 27, a deep centralized convective cover developed over the LLCC and the JTWC too upgraded Bopha into a tropical storm.[[461]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-462) By the evening of December 2, the storm entered the Philippine Area of Responsibility and was given the name Pablo.[[462]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-463) Late on December 3, the system rapidly intensified into a category 5-equivalent super typhoon, as the eye started to become well defined at 19 kilometers across.[[463]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-464) Bopha then made landfall in [Mindanao](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mindanao "Mindanao") at the same intensity.[[464]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-465) After landfall in Mindanao,[[465]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-466) Bopha weakened to a category 1-equivalent typhoon as it passed through Palawan island.[[466]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-467) On December 7, Bopha rapidly re-intensified, going from a Category 1 to a Category 4 in less than 6 hours.[[467]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-468)[[468]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-469) The next day, it weakened rapidly from a typhoon to a tropical storm due to moderate vertical wind shear.[[469]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-470) On December 9, the JTWC issued its final advisory as it weakened into tropical depression.[[470]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-471) Bopha was last noted about 70 kilometers north of Binabalian, Philippines that same day.[[471]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-472)

### Tropical Storm Wukong (Quinta)

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=30 "Edit section: Tropical Storm Wukong (Quinta)")]

Tropical storm(JMA)
Tropical storm(SSHWS)
[![Image 59](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Wukong_27w_Dec_26_2012.jpg/250px-Wukong_27w_Dec_26_2012.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Wukong_27w_Dec_26_2012.jpg)[![Image 60](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Wukong_2012_track.png/250px-Wukong_2012_track.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Wukong_2012_track.png)
Duration December 24– December 29
Peak intensity 75 km/h (45 mph) (10-min);

1000[hPa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit) "Pascal (unit)")([mbar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(unit) "Bar (unit)"))

Main article: [Tropical Storm Wukong (2012)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Wukong_(2012) "Tropical Storm Wukong (2012)")

Early on December 24, the JMA reported that a tropical depression had developed within a trough of low pressure, about 220 km (135 mi) to the north-east of [Palau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palau "Palau").[[472]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-473)[[473]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-Wukong_BT-474) During that day the depressions low level circulation gradually consolidated further, as it moved towards the west-northwest along the southern edge of the subtropical ridge of high pressure.[[474]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-475) The JTWC and PAGASA subsequently initiated advisories on the system with the latter naming it Quinta.[[475]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-476)[[476]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-477) Early on Christmas Day 2012, the JMA reported that the depression had become a tropical storm and named it as Wukong, before reporting that the system had attained its peak 10-minute sustained windspeeds of 75 km/h (45 mph).[[473]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-Wukong_BT-474) Later that day, the system passed over or close to several of the [Visayan Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Visayan_Islands "Visayan Islands"), before the JTWC reported that the system had reached its peak 1-minute sustained windspeeds of 65 km/h (35 mph).[[477]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-478)[[478]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-27W_BT-479)

During December 26, Wukong continued to move through the Philippine islands, before the JTWC reported that the system had become a tropical depression, after its low level circulation center became fully exposed within an area of moderate to strong vertical windshear.[[478]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-27W_BT-479)[[479]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-480) However, throughout December 27, as the system moved through the South China Sea and deep convection redeveloped over the systems center, the JMA continued to report that Wukong was a tropical storm.[[473]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-Wukong_BT-474)[[480]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-481) During the next day, the JMA reported that the system had weakened into a tropical depression, before the JTWC issued their final warning on Wukong as a north-easterly cold surge along the coast of south-east Asia had caused the depression to become fully exposed.[[473]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-Wukong_BT-474)[[481]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-482) The depression subsequently was last noted during the next day by both the JTWC and the JMA, dissipating about 190 km (120 mi) to the south of Vietnam.[[473]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-Wukong_BT-474)[[478]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-27W_BT-479)

Within the Philippines, 23 people were killed, while 4 others were left missing.[[482]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-483)<[[483]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-484)

### Other systems

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=31 "Edit section: Other systems")]

On April 8, the JMA started to monitor a tropical depression, that had developed about 2,000 km (1,245 mi) to the northeast of Tarawa island in Kiribati.[[484]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-485) Over the next few days the JMA continued to monitor the depression, before it was last noted by the JMA during April 11 about 450 km (280 mi) to the northwest of [Wake Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wake_Island "Wake Island").[[485]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-486) Late on April 28, the JMA reported that a tropical depression had developed about 460 km (285 mi) to the southeast of Davao City on the Philippine island of [Mindanao](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mindanao "Mindanao").[[486]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-487) Over the next day, the depression moved towards the west-northwest, before it was last noted early on April 30, as it dissipated near Mindanao.[[487]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-488)[[488]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-489)[[489]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-490)[[490]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-491)

On August 5, the Central Pacific Hurricane Center started to monitor a TUTT cell that had developed into a subtropical low, while located about 400 km (250 mi) to the southeast of [Midway Atoll](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Midway_Atoll "Midway Atoll").[[491]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-492)[[492]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-493) Over the next few days the low moved westwards towards the Western Pacific, before it moved into the basin during August 7. As it continued to move towards the west the JMA reported on August 9, that the low had developed into a tropical depression.[[493]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-494) The system re-entered the Central Pacific Ocean early on August 11.[[494]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-495) On August 23, the JMA reported that a tropical depression had developed about 441 km (275 mi) to the northeast of Shanghai in China.[[495]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-496) Over the next few days, the depression moved northwards, before it was last noted by the JMA during August 25 moving into North Korea.[[496]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-497)[[497]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-498) During September 10, the JMA started to monitor a tropical depression, that had developed in an area of moderate vertical windshear between two upper tropospheric trough cells about 945 km (585 mi) to the southeast of Tokyo, Japan.[[498]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-499)[[499]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-500) During that day the depression remained near stationary, before it started during September 11 to move northwards as it [directly interacted](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fujiwhara_effect "Fujiwhara effect") with another area of low pressure, located about 405 km (250 mi) to the northwest of the depression.[[500]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-501)[[501]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-502)[[502]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-503) Over the next couple of days, as the depression moved towards the northwest, the system transitioned into a subtropical cyclone, before it was last noted by the JMA during September 13.[[503]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-504)[[504]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-505)

Storm names
-----------

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=32 "Edit section: Storm names")]

See also: [Tropical cyclone naming](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming "Tropical cyclone naming") and [History of tropical cyclone naming](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_tropical_cyclone_naming "History of tropical cyclone naming")

Within the North-western Pacific Ocean, both the [Japan Meteorological Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency "Japan Meteorological Agency") (JMA) and the [Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration "Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration") assign names to tropical cyclones that develop in the Western Pacific, which can result in a tropical cyclone having two names.[[505]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-Padgett_Dec_99-506) The Japan Meteorological Agency's RSMC Tokyo— Typhoon Center assigns international names to tropical cyclones on behalf of the [World Meteorological Organization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization "World Meteorological Organization")'s Typhoon Committee, should they be judged to have 10-minute sustained windspeeds of 65 km/h, (40 mph).[[506]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-TC-507) While the Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration assigns names to tropical cyclones which move into or form as a tropical depression in their area of responsibility located between 135°E and 115°E and between 5°N-25°N even if the cyclone has had an international name assigned to it.[[505]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-Padgett_Dec_99-506) The names of significant tropical cyclones are retired, by both [PAGASA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_retired_Philippine_typhoon_names "List of retired Philippine typhoon names") and the [Typhoon Committee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_retired_Pacific_typhoon_names_(JMA) "List of retired Pacific typhoon names (JMA)").[[506]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-TC-507) Should the list of names for the Philippine region be exhausted then names will be taken from an auxiliary list of which the first ten are published each season. Unused names are marked in gray.

### International names

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=33 "Edit section: International names")]

Main article: [List of retired Pacific typhoon names](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_retired_Pacific_typhoon_names "List of retired Pacific typhoon names")

During the season 25 tropical storms developed in the Western Pacific and each one was named by the JMA, when the system was judged to have 10-minute sustained windspeeds of 65 km/h (40 mph). The JMA selected the names from a list of 140 names, that had been developed by the 14 members nations and territories of the [ESCAP/WMO Typhoon Committee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_retired_Pacific_typhoon_names#Background "List of retired Pacific typhoon names"). During the season the names [_Pakhar_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Pakhar_(2012) "Tropical Storm Pakhar (2012)"), [_Doksuri_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Doksuri_(2012) "Tropical Storm Doksuri (2012)"), [_Haikui_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Haikui_(2012) "Typhoon Haikui (2012)"), [_Sanba_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Sanba "Typhoon Sanba"), [Maliksi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Maliksi_(2012) "Tropical Storm Maliksi (2012)") and [_Son-Tinh_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Son-Tinh "Typhoon Son-Tinh") were used for the first time, after they had replaced the names [_Matsa_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Matsa "Typhoon Matsa"), [_Nabi_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Nabi "Typhoon Nabi"), [_Longwang_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Longwang "Typhoon Longwang"), [_Chanchu_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Chanchu "Typhoon Chanchu"), [_Bilis_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Bilis "Tropical Storm Bilis") and [_Saomai_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Saomai "Typhoon Saomai"), which were retired after the [2005](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2005_Pacific_typhoon_season "2005 Pacific typhoon season") and [2006 seasons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2006_Pacific_typhoon_season "2006 Pacific typhoon season").

[Pakhar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Pakhar_(2012) "Tropical Storm Pakhar (2012)")Sanvu[Mawar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Mawar_(2012) "Typhoon Mawar (2012)")[Guchol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Guchol_(2012) "Typhoon Guchol (2012)")Talim Doksuri[Khanun](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Khanun_(2012) "Tropical Storm Khanun (2012)")[Vicente](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Vicente "Typhoon Vicente")[Saola](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Saola_(2012) "Typhoon Saola (2012)")[Damrey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Damrey_(2012) "Typhoon Damrey (2012)")[Haikui](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Haikui_(2012) "Typhoon Haikui (2012)")Kirogi[Kai-tak](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Kai-tak_(2012) "Typhoon Kai-tak (2012)")
[Tembin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Tembin_(2012) "Typhoon Tembin (2012)")[Bolaven](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Bolaven_(2012) "Typhoon Bolaven (2012)")[Sanba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Sanba "Typhoon Sanba")[Jelawat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Jelawat_(2012) "Typhoon Jelawat (2012)")Ewiniar Maliksi[Gaemi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Gaemi_(2012) "Tropical Storm Gaemi (2012)")Prapiroon Maria[Son-Tinh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Son-Tinh "Typhoon Son-Tinh")[Bopha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Bopha "Typhoon Bopha")[Wukong](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Wukong_(2012) "Tropical Storm Wukong (2012)")

#### Retirement

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=34 "Edit section: Retirement")]

After the season the Typhoon Committee retired the names [_Vicente_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Vicente "Typhoon Vicente") and [_Bopha_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Bopha "Typhoon Bopha") from its naming lists, and in 2014 and 2015, the names were subsequently replaced with _Lan_ and _Ampil_ for future seasons.[[507]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-508)

### Philippines

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=35 "Edit section: Philippines")]

Main article: [List of retired Philippine typhoon names](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_retired_Philippine_typhoon_names "List of retired Philippine typhoon names")

[Ambo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Mawar_(2012) "Typhoon Mawar (2012)")[Butchoy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Guchol_(2012) "Typhoon Guchol (2012)")Carina Dindo[Enteng](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Khanun_(2012) "Tropical Storm Khanun (2012)")
[Ferdie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Vicente "Typhoon Vicente")[Gener](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Saola_(2012) "Typhoon Saola (2012)")[Helen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Kai-tak_(2012) "Typhoon Kai-tak (2012)")[Igme](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Tembin_(2012) "Typhoon Tembin (2012)")[Julian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Bolaven_(2012) "Typhoon Bolaven (2012)")
[Karen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Sanba "Typhoon Sanba")[Lawin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Jelawat_(2012) "Typhoon Jelawat (2012)")[Marce](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Gaemi_(2012) "Tropical Storm Gaemi (2012)")Nina[Ofel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Son-Tinh "Typhoon Son-Tinh")
[Pablo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Bopha "Typhoon Bopha")[Quinta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Wukong_(2012) "Tropical Storm Wukong (2012)")Rolly _(unused)_ Siony _(unused)_ Tonyo _(unused)_
Ulysses _(unused)_ Vicky _(unused)_ Warren _(unused)_ Yoyong _(unused)_ Zosimo _(unused)_
Auxiliary list
Alakdan _(unused)_ Baldo _(unused)_ Clara _(unused)_ Dencio _(unused)_ Estong _(unused)_
Felipe _(unused)_ Gardo _(unused)_ Heling _(unused)_ Ismael _(unused)_ Julio _(unused)_

During the season PAGASA used its own naming scheme for the 17 tropical cyclones, that either developed within or moved into their self-defined area of responsibility.[[508]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-PAGASA_Names-509) The names were taken from a list of names, that had been last used during [2008](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008_Pacific_typhoon_season "2008 Pacific typhoon season") and were used again during [2016](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016_Pacific_typhoon_season "2016 Pacific typhoon season").[[508]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-PAGASA_Names-509)

This is the same list used in 2008, except for the names [_Carina_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Talim_(2012) "Tropical Storm Talim (2012)") and [_Ferdie_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Vicente "Typhoon Vicente"), which replaced [_Cosme_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Halong_(2008) "Tropical Storm Halong (2008)") and [_Frank_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Fengshen_(2008) "Typhoon Fengshen (2008)"), respectively. Both names were used for the first time this year.

#### Retirement

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=36 "Edit section: Retirement")]

After the season, the name [_Pablo_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhoon_Bopha "Typhoon Bopha") was retired by PAGASA due to the damages and deaths caused by the storm and was replaced by _Pepito_.[[509]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-510)

Season effects
--------------

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2012_Pacific_typhoon_season&action=edit&section=37 "Edit section: Season effects")]

This table lists all the storms that developed in the western Pacific Ocean to the west of the [International Date Line](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Date_Line "International Date Line") during the 2012 season. It includes their intensity, duration, name, areas affected deaths, and damages. All damage figures are in 2012 USD. Damages and deaths from a storm include when the storm was a precursor wave, or an extratropical low.

Notes

1.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_ref-2)**The Tropical Storm Risk Consortium defines an intense typhoon as a typhoon with maximum 1-minute sustained winds greater than 175 km/h (110 mph).[[1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Pacific_typhoon_season#cite_note-TSR_May-1)
